408.01  <p>(<i>The Mabbot street entrance of nighttown, before which stretches an uncobbled

408.04  with faint rainbow fans. Round Rabaiotti's halted ice gondola stunted
408.05  men and women squabble. They grab wafers between which are wedged
408.06  lumps of coal and copper snow. Sucking, they scatter slowly. Children.
408.07  The swancomb of the gondola, highreared, forges on through the murk,
408.08  white and blue under a lighthouse. Whistles call and answer.</i>)</p>

409.03  <p>(<i>They release him. He jerks on. A pigmy woman swings on a rope slung

409.05  muffled by its arm and hat moves, groans, grinding growling teeth, and
409.06  snores again. On a step a gnome totting among a rubbishtip crouches
409.07  to shoulder a sack of rags and bones. A crone standing by with a smoky
409.08  oil lamp rams the last bottle in the maw of his sack. He heaves his
409.09  booty, tugs askew his peaked cap and hobbles off mutely. The crone
409.10  makes back for her lair swaying her lamp. A bandy child, asquat on
409.11  the doorstep with a papershuttlecock, crawls sidling after her in spurts,
409.12  clutches her skirt, scrambles up. A drunken navvy grips with both
409.13  hands the railings of an area, lurching heavily. At a corner two
409.14  night watch in shoulder capes, their hands upon their staffholsters,
409.15  loom tall. A plate crashes; a woman screams; a child wails. Oaths
409.16  of a man roar, mutter, cease. Figures wander, lurk, peer from

412.19  <p>(<i>They pass. Tommy Caffrey scrambles to a gaslamp and, clasping, climbs
412.20  in spasms. From the top spur he slides down. Jacky Caffrey clasps to
412.21  climb. The navvy lurches against the lamp. The twins scuttle off in the
412.22  dark. The navvy, swaying, presses a forefinger against a wing of his
412.23  nose and ejects from the farther nostril a long liquid jet of snot.
412.24  Shoulderiug the lamp he staggers away through the crowd with his
412.25  flaring cresset.</i></p>
412.26  <p><i>Snakes of river fog creep slowly. From drains, clefts, cesspools, middens
412.27  arise on all sides stagnant fumes. A glow leaps in the south beyond the
412.28  seaward reaches of the river. The navvy staggering forward cleaves the
412.29  crowd and lurches towards the tramsiding. On the farther side under
412.30  the railway bridge Bloom appears flushed, panting, cramming bread
412.31  and chocolate into a side pocket. From Gillen's hairdresser's window a
412.32  composite portrait shows him gallant Nelson's image. A concave mirror
413.01  at the side presents to him lovelorn longlost lugubru Booloohoom. Grave
413.02  Gladstone sees him level, Bloom for Bloom. He passes, struck by the
413.03  stare of truculent Wellington but in the convex mirror grin unstruck

414.24  <p>No thoroughfare. Close shave that but cured the stitch. Must take up
414.25  Sandow's exerciser again. On the hands down. Insure against street accident
414.26  too. The Providential. (<i>He feels his trouser pocket.</i>) Poor mamma's panacea. Heel
414.27  easily catch in tracks or bootlace in a cog. Day, the wheel of the black Maria,
414.28  peeled off my shoe at Leonard's corner. Third time is the charm. Shoe trick.
414.29  Insolent driver. I ought to report him. Tension makes them nervous. Might
415.01  be the fellow balked me this morning with that horsey woman. Same style of
415.02  beauty. Quick of him all he same. The stiff walk. True word spoken in jest.

420.01            <p><sc>the bawd</sc></p>
420.02  <p>Ten shillings a maidenhead. Fresh thing was never touched. Fifteen.
420.03  There's no-one in it only her old father that's dead drunk.</p>
420.04  <p>(<i>She points. In the gap of her dark den furtive, rainbedraggled, Bridie
420.05  Kelly stands.</i>)</p>
420.06            <p><sc>bridie</sc></p>
420.07  <p>Hatch street. Any good in your mind?</p>
420.08  <p>(<i>With a squeak she flaps her bat shawl and runs. A burly rough pursues
420.09  with booted strides. He stumbles on the steps, recovers, plunges into
420.10  gloom. Weak squeaks of laughter are heard, weaker.</i>)</p>
420.11            <p><sc>the bawd</sc></p>
420.12  <p>(<i>Her wolfeyes shining.</i>) He's getting his pleasure. You won't get a virgin in
420.13  the flash houses. Ten shillings. Don't be all night before the polis in plain
420.14  clothes sees us. Sixtyseven is a bitch.</p>
420.15  <p>(<i>Leering, Gerty MacDowell limps forward. She draws from behind,
420.16  ogling, and shows coyly her bloodied clout.</i>)</p>
420.17            <p><sc>gerty</sc></p>
420.18  <p>With all my worldly goods I thee and thou. (<i>She murmurs.</i>) You did
420.19  that. I hate you.</p>
420.20            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
420.21  <p>I? When? You're dreaming. I never saw you.</p>
420.22            <p><sc>the bawd</sc></p>
420.23  <p>Leave the gentleman alone, you cheat. Writing the gentleman false letters.
420.24  Streetwalking and soliciting. Better for your mother take the strap to you at
420.25  the bedpost, hussy like you.</p>
420.26            <p><sc>gerty</sc></p>
420.27  <p>(<i>To Bloom.</i>) When you saw all the secrets of my bottom drawer. (<i>She
420.28  paws his sleeve, slobbering.</i>) Dirty married man! I love you for doing that to me.</p>
420.29  <p>(<i>She slides away crookedly. Mrs Breen in man's frieze overcoat with loose
421.01  bellows pockets, stands in the causeway, her roguish eyes wideopen,
421.02  smiling in all her herbivorous buckteeth.</i>)</p>
421.03            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
421.04  <p>Mr ...</p>
421.05            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
421.06  <p>(<i>Coughs gravely.</i>) Madam, when we last had this pleasure by letter dated
421.07  the sixteenth instant ...</p>
421.08            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
421.09  <p>Mr Bloom! You down here in the haunts of sin! I caught you nicely!
421.10  Scamp!</p>
421.11            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
421.12  <p>(<i>Hurriedly.</i>) Not so loud my name. Whatever do you think me? Don't
421.13  give me away. Walls have hears. How do you do? It's ages since I. You're
421.14  looking splendid. Absolutely it. Seasonable weather we are having this time of
421.15  year. Black refracts heat. Short cut home here. Interesting quarter. Rescue of
421.16  fallen women Magdalen asylum. I am the secretary ...</p>
421.17            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
421.18  <p>(<i>Holds up a finger.</i>) Now don't tell a big fib! I know somebody won't like
421.19  that. O just wait till I see Molly! (<i>Slily.</i>) Account for yourself this very
421.20  sminute or woe betide you!</p>
421.21            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
421.22  <p>(<i>Looks behind.</i>) She often said she'd like to visit. Slumming. The exotic,
421.23  you see. Negro servants too in livery if she had money. Othello black brute.
421.24  Eugene Stratton. Even the bones and cornerman at the Livermore christies.
421.25  Bohee brothers. Sweep for that matter.</p>
421.26  <p>(<i>Tom and Sam Bohee, coloured coons in white duck suits, scarlet socks,
421.27  upstarched Sambo chokers and large scarlet asters in their buttonholes
421.28  leap out. Each has his banjo slung. Their paler smaller negroid hands
421.29  jingle the twingtwang wires. Flashing white Kaffir eyes and tusks
421.30  they rattle through a breakdown in clumsy clogs, twinging, singing,
421.31  back to back, toe heel, heel toe, with smackfatclacking nigger lips.</i>)</p>
422.01            <p><sc>tom and sam</sc></p>
422.02  <p>There's someone in the house with Dina</p>
422.03  <p>There's someone in the house, I know,</p>
422.04  <p>There's someone in the house with Dina</p>
422.05  <p>Playing on the old banjo.</p>
422.06  <p>(<i>They whisk black masks from raw babby faces: then, chuckling, chortling,
422.07  trumming, twanging they diddle diddle cakewalk dance away.</i>)</p>
422.08            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
422.09  <p>(<i>With a sour tenderish smile.</i>) A little frivol, shall we, if you are so
422.10  inclined? Would you like me perhaps to embrace you just for a fraction of
422.11  a second?</p>
422.12            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
422.13  <p>(<i>Screams gaily.</i>) O, you ruck! You ought to see yourself!</p>
422.14            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
422.15  <p>For old sake' sake. I only meant a square party, a mixed marriage mingling
422.16  of our different little conjugials. You know I had a soft corner for you.
422.17  (<i>Gloomily.</i>) 'Twas I sent you that valentine of the dear gazelle.</p>
422.18            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
422.19  <p>Glory Alice, you do look a holy show! Killing simply. (<i>She puts out her
422.20  hand inquisitively.</i>) What are you hiding behind your back? Tell us, there's a
422.21  dear.</p>
422.22            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
422.23  <p>(<i>Seizes her wrist with his free hand.</i>) Josie Powell that was, prettiest deb in
422.24  Dublin. How time flies by! Do you remember, harking back in a retrospective
422.25  arrangement, Old Christmas night Georgina Simpson's housewarming while
422.26  they were playing the Irving Bishop game, finding the pin blindfold and
422.27  thoughtreading! Subject, what is in this snuffbox!</p>
422.28            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
422.29  <p>You were the lion of the night with your seriocomic recitation and you
422.30  looked the part. You were always a favourite with the ladies.</p>
423.01            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
423.02  <p>(<i>Squire of dames, in dinner jacket with watered silkfacings, blue masonic badge
423.03  in his buttonhole, black bow and mother-of-pear studs, a prismatic champagne glass

423.05            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
423.06  <p>The dear dead days beyond recall. Love's old sweet song.</p>
423.07            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
423.08  <p>(<i>Meaningfully dropping his voice.</i>) I confess I'm teapot with curiosity to find
423.09  out whether some person's something is a little teapot at present.</p>
423.10            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
423.11  <p>(<i>Gushingly.</i>) Tremendously teapot! London's teapot and I'm simply teapot
423.12  all over me. (<i>She rubs sides with him.</i>) After the parlour mystery games and the
423.13  crackers from the tree we sat on the staircase ottoman. Under the mistletoe.
423.14  Two is company.</p>
423.15            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
423.16  <p>(<i>Wearing a purple Napoleon hat with an amber halfmoon, his fingers and thumb
423.17  passing slowly down to her soft moist meaty palm which she surrenders gently.</i>) The
423.18  witching hour of night. I took the splinter out of this hand, carefully, slowly.
423.19  (<i>Tenderly, as he slips on her finger a ruby ring.</i>) <i>Là ci darem la mano.</i></p>
423.20            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
423.21  <p>(<i>In a onepiece evening frock executed in moonlight blue, a tinsel sylph's diadem
423.22  on her brow with her dancecard fallen beside her moonblue satin slipper, curves her
423.23  palm softly, breathing quickly.</i>) <i>Voglio e non.</i> You're hot! You're scalding! The
423.24  left hand nearest the heart.</p>
423.25            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
423.26  <p>When you made your present choice they said it was beauty and the beast.
423.27  I can never forgive you for that. (<i>His clenched fist at his brow.</i>) Think what it
423.28  means. All you meant to me then. (<i>Hoarsely.</i>) Woman, it's breaking me!</p>
423.29  <p>(<i>Denis Breen, whitetallhatted, with Wisdom Hely's sandwichboard, shuffles
423.30  past them in carpet slippers, his dull beard thrust out, muttering to
424.01  right and left. Little Alf Bergan, cloaked in the pall of the ace of
424.02  spades dogs him to left and right, doubled in laughter.</i>)</p>
424.03            <p><sc>alf bergan</sc></p>
424.04  <p>(<i>Points jeering at the sandwich boards.</i>) U.p: Up.</p>
424.05            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
424.06  <p>(<i>To Bloom.</i>) High jinks below stairs. (<i>She gives him the glad eye.</i>) Why
424.07  didn't you kiss the spot to make it well! You wanted to.</p>
424.08            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
424.09  <p>(<i>Shocked.</i>) Molly's best friend! Could you?</p>
424.10            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
424.11  <p>(<i>Her pulpy tongue between her lips, offers a pigeon kiss.</i>) Hnhn. The answer
424.12  is a lemon. Have you a little present for me there?</p>
424.13            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
424.14  <p>(<i>Offhandedly.</i>) Kosher. A snack for supper. The home without potted meat

424.16  Shakespeare. Unfortunately threw away the programme. Rattling good place
424.17  round there for pig's feet. Feel.</p>
424.18  <p>(<i>Richie Goulding, three ladies' hats pinned on his head, appears weighted

425.07            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
425.08  <p>(<i>Points to the navvy.</i>) A spy. Don't attract attention. I hate stupid crowds.

425.10            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
425.11  <p>Humbugging and deluthering as per usual with your cock and bull story.</p>

425.19            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>

425.23            <p><sc>the bawd</sc></p>
425.24  <p>Jewman's melt!</p>
425.25            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
425.26  <p>(<i>In an oatmeal sporting suit, a sprig of woodbine in the lapel, tony buff shirt,
425.27  shepherd's plaid Saint Andrew's cross scarftie, white spats, fawn dustcoat on his
426.01  arm, tawny red brogues, fieldglasses in bandolier and a grey billycock hat.</i>) Do you
426.02  remember a long long time, years and years ago, just after Milly, Marionette we

426.04            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
426.05  <p>(<i>In smart Saxe tailormade, white velours hat and spider veil.</i>) Leopardstown.</p>
426.06            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
426.07  <p>I mean, Leopardstown. And Molly won seven shillings on a three year old
426.08  named Nevertell and coming home along by Foxrock in that old fiveseater
426.09  shanderadan of a waggonette you were in your heyday then and you had on
426.10  that new hat of white velours with a surround of molefur that Mrs Hayes
426.11  advised you to buy because it was marked down to nineteen and eleven, a bit
426.12  of wire and an old rag of velveteen, and I'll lay you what you like she did it
426.13  on purpose ...</p>
426.14            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
426.15  <p>She did, of course, the cat! Don't tell me! Nice adviser!</p>
426.16            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
426.17  <p>Because it didn't suit you one quarter as well as the other ducky little
426.18  tammy toque with the bird of paradise wing in it that I admired on you and
426.19  you honestly looked just too fetching in it though it was a pity to kill it,
426.20  you cruel creature, little mite of a thing with a heart the size of a fullstop.</p>
426.21            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
426.22  <p>(<i>Squeezes his arm, simpers.</i>) Naughty cruel I was.</p>
426.23            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
426.24  <p>(<i>Low, secretly, ever more rapidly.</i>) And Molly was eating a sandwich of
426.25  spiced beef out of Mrs Joe Gallaher's lunch basket. Frankly, though she had
426.26  her advisers or admirers, I never cared much for her style. She was ...</p>
426.27            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
426.28  <p>Too ...</p>
426.29            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
426.30  <p>Yes. And Molly was laughing because Rogers and Maggot O'Reilly were
427.01  mimicking a cock as we passed a farmhouse and Marcus Tertius Moses, the tea
427.02  merchant, drove past us in a gig with his daughter, Dancer Moses was her
427.03  name, and the poodle in her lap bridled up and you asked me if I ever heard
427.04  or read or knew or came across ...</p>
427.05            <p><sc>mrs breen</sc></p>
427.06  <p>(<i>Eagerly.</i>) Yes, yes, yes, yes, yes, yes, yes.</p>
427.07  <p>(<i>She fades from his side. Followed by the whining dog he walks on towards
427.08  hellsgates. In an archway a standing woman, bent forward, her feet
427.09  apart, pisses cowily. Outside a shuttered pub a bunch of loiterers
427.10  listen to a tale which their broken snouted gaffer rasps out with raucous
427.11  humour. An armless pair of them flop wrestling, growling, in
427.12  maimed sodden playfight.</i>)</p>
427.13            <p><sc>the gaffer</sc></p>
427.14  <p>(<i>Crouches, his voice twisted in his snout.</i>) And when Cairns came down from
427.15  the scaffolding in Beaver Street what was he after doing it into only into the

427.17  plasterers.</p>
427.18            <p><sc>the loiterers</sc></p>
427.19  <p>(<i>Guffaw with cleft palates.</i>) O jays!</p>
427.20  <p>(<i>Their paintspeckled hats wag. Spattered with size and lime of their lodges

427.22            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
427.23  <p>Coincidence too. They think it funny. Anything but that. Broad daylight.
427.24  Trying to walk. Lucky no woman.</p>
427.25            <p><sc>the loiterers</sc></p>
427.26  <p>Jays, that's a good one. Glauber salts. O jays, into the men's porter.</p>
427.27  <p>(<i>Bloom passes. Cheap whores, singly, coupled, shawled, dishevelled, call

428.01            <p><sc>the whores</sc></p>

428.03  <p>How's your middle leg?</p>
428.04  <p>Got a match on you?</p>
428.05  <p>Eh, come her till I stiffen it for you.</p>
428.06  <p>(<i>He plodges through their sump towards the lighted street beyond. From a

428.17            <p><sc>private carr</sc></p>

428.21            <p><sc>private carr</sc></p>

428.26            <p><sc>private compton</sc></p>

429.01            <p><sc>private carr</sc></p>
429.02  <p>Bennett? He's my pal. I love old Bennett.</p>
429.03            <p><sc>the navvy</sc></p>
429.04  <p>(<i>Shouts.</i>)</p>
429.05  <p>The galling chain.</p>
429.06  <p>And free our native land.</p>
429.07  <p>(<i>He staggers forward, dragging them with him. Bloom stops, at fault.
429.08  The dog approches, his tongue outlolling, panting.</i>)</p>
429.09            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
429.10  <p>Wildgoose chase this. Disorderly houses. Lord knows where they are
429.11  gone. Drunks cover distance double quick. Nice mixup. Scene at Westland
429.12  row. Then jump in first class with third ticket. Then too far. Train with
429.13  engine behind. Might have taken me to Malahide or a siding for the night or
429.14  collision. Second drink does it. Once is a dose. What am I following him for?
429.15  Still, he's the best of that lot. If I hadn't heard about Mrs Beaufoy Purefoy
429.16  I wouldn't have gone and wouldn't have met. Kismet. He'll lose that cash.
429.17  Relieving office here. Good biz for cheapjacks, organs. What do ye lack?
429.18  Soon got, soon gone. Might have lost my life too with that mangong-
429.19  wheeltracktrolleyglarejuggernaut only for presence of mind. Can't always save
429.20  you, though. If I had passed Truelock's window that day two minutes later
429.21  would have been shot. Absence of body. Still if bullet only went through my
429.22  coat get damages for shock, five hundred pounds. What was he? Kildare street
429.23  club toff. God help his gamekeeper.</p>
429.24  <p>(<i>He gazes ahead reading on the wall a scrawled chalk legend</i> Wet Dream
429.25  <i>and a phallic design.</i>)</p>
429.26  <p>Odd! Molly drawing on the frosted carriagepane at Kingstown. What's
429.27  that like? (<i>Gaudy dollwomen loll in the lighted doorways, in window embrasures,
429.28  smoking birdseye cigarettes. The odour of the sicksewet weed floats towards him in slow
429.29  round ovalling wreaths.</i>)</p>
429.30            <p><sc>the wreaths</sc></p>
429.31  <p>Sweet are the sweets. Sweets of sin.</p>
429.32            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
429.33  <p>My spine's a bit limp. Go or turn? And this food? Eat it and get all
430.01  pigsticky. Absurd I am. Waste of money. One and eight pence too much.
430.02  (<i>The retriever drives a cold snivelling muzzle against his hand, wagging his tail.</i>)
430.03  Strange how they take to me. Even that brute today. Better speak to him first.
430.04  Like women they like <i>rencontres</i>. Stinks like a polecat. <i>Chacun son go|<ut.</i> He
430.05  might be mad. Fido. Uncertain in his movements. Good fellow! Garryowen!
430.06  (<i>The wolfdog sprawls on his back, wriggling obscenely with begging paws, his long
430.07  black tongue lolling out.</i>) Influence of his surroundings. Give and have done
430.08  with it. Provided nobody. (<i>Calling encouraging words he shambles back with a
430.09  furtive poacher's tread, dogged by the setter into a dark stalestunk corner. He
430.10  unrolls one parcel and goes to dump the crubeen softly but holds back and feels the
430.11  trotter.</i>) Sizeable for threepence. But then I have it in my left hand. Calls for
430.12  more effort. Why? Smaller from want of use. O, let it slide. Two and six.</p>
430.13  <p>(<i>With regret he lets unrolled crubeen and trotter slide. The mastiff mauls

430.16  murmur together.</i>)</p>
430.17            <p><sc>the watch</sc></p>
430.18  <p>Bloom. Of Bloom. For Bloom. Bloom.</p>
430.19  <p>(<i>Each lays hand on Bloom's shoulder.</i>)</p>
430.20            <p><sc>first watch</sc></p>
430.21  <p>Caught in the act. Commit no nuisance.</p>
430.22            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
430.23  <p>(<i>Stammers.</i>) I am doing good to others.</p>
430.24  <p><i>(A covey of gulls, storm petrels, rises hungrily from Liffey slime with
430.25  Banbury cakes in their beaks.)</i></p>
430.26            <p><sc>the gulls</sc></p>
430.27  <p>Kaw kave kankury kake.</p>
430.28            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
430.29  <p>The friend of man. Trained by kindness.</p>
430.30  <p>(<i>He points. Bob Doran, toppling from a high barstool, sways over the
430.31  munching spaniel.</i>)</p>
431.01            <p><sc>bob doran</sc></p>
431.02  <p>Towser. Give us the paw. Give the paw.</p>
431.03  <p>(<i>The bulldog growls, his scruff standing, a gobbet of pig's knuckle between
431.04  his molars through which rabid scumspittle dribbles. Bob Doran falls
431.05  silently into an area.</i>)</p>
431.06            <p><sc>second watch</sc></p>
431.07  <p>Prevention of cruelty to animals.</p>
431.08            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
431.09  <p>(<i>Enthusiastically.</i>) A noble work! I scolded that tramdriver on Harold's
431.10  cross bridge for illusing the poor horse with his harness scab. Bad French I got
431.11  for my pains. Of course it was frosty and the last tram. All tales of circus life
431.12  are highly demoralising.</p>
431.13  <p>(<i>Signor Maffei, passion pale, in liontamer's costume with diamonds studs
431.14  in his shirtfront steps forward, holding a circus paper hoop, a curling
431.15  carriagewhip and a revolver with which he covers the gorging
431.16  boarhound.</i></p>
431.17            <p><sc>signor maffei</sc></p>
431.18  <p>(<i>With a sinister smile.</i>) Ladies and gentlemen, my educated greyhound. It
431.19  was I broke in the bucking broncho Ajax with my patent spiked saddle for
431.20  carnivores. Lash under the belly with a knotted thong. Block tackle and a
431.21  strangling pully will bring your lion to heel, no matter how fractious, even
431.22  <i>Leo ferox</i> there, the Libyan maneater. A redhot crowbar and some liniment
431.23  rubbing on the burning part produced Fritz of Amsterdam, the thinking hyena.
431.24  (<i>He glares.</i>) I possess the Indian sign. The glint of my eye does it with these
431.25  breastsparklers. (<i>With a bewitching smile.</i>) I now introduce Mademoiselle Ruby,
431.26  the pride of the ring.</p>
431.27            <p><sc>first watch</sc></p>
431.28  <p>Come. Name and address.</p>
431.29            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
431.30  <p>I have forgotten for the moment. Ah, yes! (<i>He takes off his high grade hat,
431.31  saluting.</i>) Dr Bloom, Leopold, dental surgeon. You have heard of von Bloom
431.32  Pasha. Umpteen millions. <i>Donnerwetter!</i> Owns half Austria. Egypt. Cousin.</p>
432.01            <p><sc>first watch</sc></p>

432.17  know that old joke, rose of Castile. Bloom. The change of name. Virag. (<i>He
432.18  murmurs privately and confidentially.</i>) We are engaged you see, sergeant. Lady
432.19  in the case. Love entanglement. (<i>He shoulders the second watch gently.</i>) Dash it
432.20  all. It's a way we gallants have in the navy. Uniform that does it. (<i>He turns
432.21  gravely to the first watch.</i>) Still, of course, you do get your Waterloo sometimes.
432.22  Drop in some evening and have a glass of old Burgundy. (<i>To the second watch
432.23  gaily.</i>) I'll introduce you, inspector. She's game. Do it in the shake of a lamb's

432.25  <p>(<i>A dark mercurialised face appears, leading a veiled figure.</i>)</p>

432.28            <p><sc>martha</sc></p>

433.01            <p><sc>first watch</sc></p>
433.02  <p>(<i>Sternly.</i>) Come to the station.</p>
433.03            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
433.04  <p>(<i>Scared, hats himself, steps back then, plucking at his heart and lifting his
433.05  right forearm on the square, he gives the sign and dueguard of fellowcraft.</i>) No, no,
433.06  worshipful master, light of love. Mistaken identity. The Lyons mail. Lesurques
433.07  and Dubosc. You remember the Childs fratricide case. We medical men. By
433.08  striking him dead with a hatchet, I am wrongfully accused. Better one guilty
433.09  escape than ninetynine wrongfully condemned.</p>
433.10            <p><sc>martha</sc></p>
433.11  <p>(<i>Sobbing behind her veil.</i>) Breach of promise. My real name is Peggy Griffin.
433.12  He wrote to me that he was miserable. I'll tell my brother, the Bective
433.13  rugger fullback, on you, heartless flirt.</p>
433.14            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
433.15  <p>(<i>Behind his hand.</i>) She's drunk. The woman is inebriated. (<i>He murmurs

433.17            <p><sc>second watch</sc></p>
433.18  <p>(<i>Tears in his eyes, to Bloom.</i>) You ought to be thoroughly well ashamed of

433.20            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
433.21  <p>Gentlemen of the jury, let me explain. A pure mare's nest. I am a man
433.22  misunderstood. I am being made a scapegoat of. I am a respectable married man,
433.23  without a stain on my character. I live in Eccles street. My wife, I am the
433.24  daughter of a most distinguished commander, a gallant upstanding gentleman,
433.25  what do you call him, Majorgeneral Brian Tweedy, one of Britain's fighting
433.26  men who helped to win our battles. Got his majority for the heroic defence
433.27  of Rorke's Drift.</p>
433.28            <p><sc>first watch</sc></p>
433.29  <p>Regiment.</p>
433.30            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>

433.32  known the world over. I think I see some old comrades in arms up there
434.01  among you. The R.D.F. With our own Metropolitan police, guardians of
434.02  our homes, the pluckiest lads and the finest body of men, as physique, in the

434.04            <p><sc>a voice</sc></p>

434.28  <p>(<i>Mr Philip Beaufoy, palefaced, stands in the witnessbox, in accurate

435.01            <p><sc>beaufoy</sc></p>

435.04  of a gentleman would stoop to such particularly loathsome conduct. One of

435.06  perfectly obvious that with the most inherent baseness he has cribbed some of
435.07  my bestselling books, really gorgeous stuff, a perfect gem, the love passages in
435.08  which are beneath suspicion. The Beaufoy books of love and great possessions
435.09  with which your lordship is doubtless familiar, are a household word

435.18  Mr J.B. Pinker is in attendance. I presume, my lord, we shall receive the usual

437.20  <p>(<i>Clerk of the crown and peace, resonantly.</i>) Order in court! The accused will
437.21  now make a bogus statement.</p>
437.22  <p>(<i>Bloom, pleading not guilty and holding a fullblown waterlily, begins a
437.23  long unintelligible speech. They would hear what counsel had to say
437.24  in his stirring address to the grandjury. He was down and out but,
437.25  through branded as a black sheep, if he might say so, he meant to reform,
437.26  to retrieve the memory of the past in a purely sisterly way and return to
437.27  nature as a purely domestic animal. A seven months child he had been
437.28  carefully brought up and nurtured by an aged bedridden parent. There
437.29  might have been lapses of an erring father but he wanted to turn over
437.30  a new leaf and now, when at long last in sight of the whipping post, to
437.31  lead a homely life in the evening of his days, permeated by the affectionate
438.01  surroundings of the heaving bosom of the family. An acclimatised
438.02  Britisher, he had seen that summer eve from the footplate of an engine
438.03  cab of the Loop line railway company while the rain refrained from
438.04  falling glimpses, as it were, through the windows of loveful households
438.05  in Dublin city and urban district of scenes truly rural of happiness of
438.06  the better land with Dockrell's wallpaper at one and ninepence a dozen,
438.07  innocent Britishborn bairns lisping prayers to the Sacred Infant, youthful
438.08  scholars grappling with their pensums, model young ladies playing on the
438.09  pianoforte or anon all with fervour reciting the family rosary round
438.10  the crackling Yulelog while in the boreens and green lanes the colleens
438.11  with their swains strolled what times the strains of the organtoned
438.12  melodeon Brittania metalbound with four acting stops and twelvefold
438.13  bellows, a sacrifice, greatest bargain ever ...</i>)</p>

438.21  <p>(<i>The crossexamination proceeds</i> re <i>Bloom and the bucket. A large bucket.

438.30            <p><sc>j.j. o'molloy</sc></p>
438.31  <p>(<i>In barrister's grey wig and stuffgown, speaking with a voice of pained protest.</i>)
438.32  This is no place for indecent levity at the expense of an erring mortal
438.33  disguised in liquor. We are not in a beargarden nor at an Oxford rag nor is this
439.01  a travesty of justice. My client is an infant, a poor foreign immigrant who
439.02  started scratch as a stowaway and is now trying to turn an honest penny. The
439.03  trumped up misdemeanour was due to a momentary aberration of heredity,
439.04  brought on by hallucination, such familiarities as the alleged guilty occurrence
439.05  being quite permitted in my client's native place, the land of the Pharaoh.
439.06  <i>Prima facie,</i> I put it to you that there was no attempt at carnally knowing.
439.07  Intimacy did not occur and the offence complained of by Driscoll, that her
439.08  virtue was solicited, was not repeated. I would deal in especial with atavism.
439.09  There have been cases of shipwreck and somnambulism in my client's family.
439.10  If the accused could speak he could a tale unfold one of the strangest that
439.11  have ever been narrated between the covers of a book. He himself, my lord,
439.12  is a physical wreck from cobbler's weak chest. His submission is that he is of
439.13  Mongolian extraction and irresponsible for his actions. Not all there, in fact.</p>
439.14            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
439.15  <p>(<i>Barefoot, pigeonbreasted, in lascar's vest and trousers, apologetic toes turned in,
439.16  opens his tiny mole's eyes and looks about him dazedly, passing a slow hand across
439.17  his forehead. Then he hitches his belt sailor fashion and with a shrug of oriental
439.18  obeisance salutes the court, pointing one thumb heavenward.</i>) Him makee velly
439.19  muchee fine night. (<i>He begins to lilt simply.</i>)</p>
439.20  <p>Li li poo lil chile.</p>
439.21  <p>Blingee pigfoot evly night.</p>
439.22  <p>Payee two shilly ...</p>

439.24            <p><sc>j.j. o'molloy</sc></p>
439.25  <p>(<i>Hotly to the populace.</i>) This is a lonehand fight. By Hades, I will not have
439.26  any client of mine gagged and badgered in this fashion by a pack of curs and
439.27  laughing hyenas. The Mosaic code has superseded the law of the jungle.
439.28  I say it and I say it emphatically without wishing for one moment
439.29  to defeat the ends of justice, accused, was not accessory before the act and
439.30  prosecutrix has not been tampered with. The young person was treated by
439.31  defendant as if she were his very own daughter. (<i>Bloom takes J.J. O'Molloy's
439.32  hand and raises it to his lips.</i>) I shall call rebutting evidence to prove up to the
439.33  hilt that the hidden hand is again at its old game. When in doubt persecute
439.34  Bloom. My client, an innately bashful man, would be the last man in the
439.35  world to do anything ungentlemanly which injured modesty could object to
440.01  or cast a stone at a girl who took the wrong turning when some dastard,
440.02  responsible for her condition, had worked his own sweet will on her. He wants
440.03  to go straight. I regard him as the whitest man I know. He is down on his
440.04  luck at present owing to the mortgaging of his extensive property at Agendath
440.05  Netaim in faraway Asia Minor, slides of which will now be shown. (<i>To Bloom.</i>)
440.06  I suggest that you will do the handsome thing.</p>

440.31  I have moved in the charmed circle of the highest ... Queens of Dublin Society.

441.01            <p><sc>mrs yelverton barry</sc></p>
441.02  <p>(<i>In lowcorsaged opal balldress and elbowlength ivory gloves, wearing a
441.03  sabletrimmed brick quilted dolman, a comb of brilliants and panache of osprey in
441.04  her hair.</i>) Arrest him, constable. He wrote me an anonymous letter in prentice
441.05  backhand when my husband was in the North Riding of Tipperary on the
441.06  Munster circuit, signed James Lovebirch. He said that he had seen from the
441.07  gods my peerless globes as I sat in a box of the <i>Theatre Royal</i> at a command
441.08  performance of <i>La Cigale</i>. I deeply inflamed him, he said. He made improper
441.09  overtures to me to misconduct myself at half past four p.m. on the following
441.10  Thursday, Dunsink time. He offered to send me through the post a work of
441.11  fiction by Monsieur Paul de Kock, entitled <i>The Girl with the Three Pairs of
441.12  Stays</i>.</p>
441.13            <p><sc>mrs bellingham</sc></p>
441.14  <p>(<i>In cap and seal coney mantle, wrapped up to the nose, steps out of her brougham
441.15  and scans through tortoiseshell quizzing-glasses which she takes from inside her huge
441.16  opossum muff.</i>) Also to me. Yes, I believe it is the same objectionable person.
441.17  Because he closed my carriage door outside sir Thornley Stoker's one sleety day
441.18  during the cold snap of February ninetythree when even the grid of the wastepipe
441.19  and ballstop in my bath cistern were frozen. Subsequently he enclosed a bloom
441.20  of edelweiss culled on the heights, as he said, in my honour. I had it examined
441.21  by a botanical expert and elicited the information that it was a blossom of the
441.22  homegrown potato plant purloined from a forcingcase of the model farm.</p>
441.23            <p><sc>mrs yelverton barry</sc></p>
441.24  <p>Shame on him!</p>
441.25  <p>(<i>A crowd of sluts and ragamuffins surges forward.</i>)</p>
441.26            <p><sc>the sluts and ragamuffins</sc></p>
441.27  <p>(<i>Screaming.</i>) Stop thief! Hurrah there, Bluebeard! Three cheers for
441.28  Ikey Mo!</p>
441.29            <p><sc>second watch</sc></p>
441.30  <p>(<i>Produces handcuffs.</i>) Here are the darbies.</p>
441.31            <p><sc>mrs bellingham</sc></p>
441.32  <p>He addressed me in several handwritings with fulsome compliments as a
442.01  Venus in furs and alleged profound pity for my frostbound coachman Palmer
442.02  while in the same breath he expressed himself as envious of his earflaps and
442.03  ffeecy sheepskins and of his fortunate proximity to my person, when standing
442.04  behind my chair wearing my livery and the armorial bearings of the Bellingham
442.05  escutcheon garnished sable, a buck's head couped or. He lauded almost
442.06  extravagantly my nether extremities, my swelling calves in silk hose drawn up
442.07  to the limit and eulogised glowingly my other hidden treasures in priceless
442.08  lace which, he said, he could conjure up. He urged me, stating that he felt it
442.09  his mission in life to urge me, to defile the marriage bed, to commit adultery
442.10  at the earliest possible opportunity.</p>
442.11            <p><sc>the honourable mrs mervyn talboys</sc></p>
442.12  <p>(<i>In amazon costume, hard hat, jackboots cockspurred, vermilion waistcoat, fawn
442.13  musketeer gauntlets with braided drums, long train held up and hunting crop with
442.14  which she strikes her welt constantly.</i>) Also me. Because he saw me on the polo
442.15  ground of the Phœnix park at the match All Ireland versus the Rest of Ireland.
442.16  My eyes, I know, shone divinely as I watched Captain Slogger Dennehy of
442.17  the Inniskillings win the final chukkar on his darling cob <i>Centaur</i>. This
442.18  plebeian Don Juan observed me from behind a hackney car and sent me in
442.19  double envelopes an obscene photograph, such as are sold after dark on Paris
442.20  boulevards, insulting to any lady. I have it still. It represents a partially nude
442.21  se|?norita, frail and lovely (his wife as he solemnly assured me, taken by him
442.22  from nature) practising illicit intercourse with a muscular torero, evidently a
442.23  blackguard. He urged me to do likewise, to misbehave, to sin with officers of
442.24  the garrison. He implored me to soil his letter in an unspeakable manner, to
442.25  chastise him as he richly deserves, to bestride and ride him, to give him a most
442.26  vicious horsewhipping.</p>
442.27            <p><sc>mrs bellingham</sc></p>

442.29            <p><sc>mrs yelverton barry</sc></p>
442.30  <p>Me too.</p>

443.01            <p><sc>the honourable mrs mervyn talboys</sc></p>

443.11            <p><sc>mrs bellingham</sc></p>

443.15            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
443.16  <p>All these people. I meant only the spanking idea. A warm tingling glow
443.17  without effusion. Refined birching to stimulate the circulation.</p>
443.18            <p><sc>the honourable mrs mervyn talboys</sc></p>
443.19  <p>(<i>Laughs derisively.</i>) O, did you, my fine fellow? Well, by the living God,

443.23            <p><sc>mrs bellingham</sc></p>

443.27            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>

444.01            <p><sc>mrs yelverton barry</sc></p>

448.01            <p><sc>paddy dignam</sc></p>

451.01            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
451.02  <p>(<i>Forlornly.</i>) I never loved a dear gazelle but it was sure to ...</p>
451.03  <p>(<i>Gazelles are leaping, feeding on the mountains. Near are lakes. Round
451.04  their shores file shadows black of cedargroves. Aroma rises, a strong
451.05  hairgrowth of resin. It burns, the orient, a sky of sapphire, cleft by the

451.29  (<i>Lewdly.</i>) The mouth can be better engaged than with a cylinder of rank weed.</p>
452.01            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
452.02  <p>Go on. Make a stump speech out of it.</p>
452.03            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
452.04  <p>(<i>In workman's corduroy overalls, black gansy with red floating tie and apache
452.05  cap.</i>) Mankind is incorrigible. Sir Walter Raleigh brought from the new world
452.06  that potato and that weed, the one a killer of pestilence by absorption, the other
452.07  a poisoner of the ear, eye, heart, memory, will, understanding, all. That is to
452.08  say, he brought the poison a hundred years before another person whose
452.09  name I forget brought the food. Suicide. Lies. All our habits. Why, look at our
452.10  public life!</p>
452.11  <p>(<i>Midnight chimes from distant steeples.</i>)</p>
452.12            <p><sc>the chimes</sc></p>

452.14            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
452.15  <p>(<i>In alderman's gown and chain.</i>) Electors of Arran Quay, Inns Quay,
452.16  Rotunda, Mountjoy and North Dock better run a tramline, I say, from the
452.17  cattlemarket to the river. That's the music of the future. That's my programme.
452.18  <i>Cui bono?</i> But our bucaneering Vanderdeckens in their phantom ship of
452.19  finance ...</p>
452.20            <p><sc>an elector</sc></p>

452.22  <p>(<i>The aurora borealis of the torchlight procession leaps.</i>)</p>

452.24  <p>Hooray!</p>
452.25  <p>(<i>Several wellknown burgesses, city magnates and freemen of the city shake
452.26  hands with Bloom and congratulate him. Timothy Harrington, late
452.27  thrice Lord Mayor of Dublin, imposing in mayoral scarlet, gold chain
452.28  and white silk tie, confers with councillor Lorcan Sherlock, locum
452.29  tenens. They nod vigorously in agreement.</i>)</p>
453.01            <p><sc>late lord mayor harrington</sc></p>
453.02  <p>(<i>In scarlet robe with mace, gold mayoral chain and large white silk scarf.</i>)
453.03  That alderman, sir Leo Bloom's speech be printed at the expense of the
453.04  ratepayers. That the house in which he was born be ornamented with a
453.05  commemorative tablet and that the thoroughfare hitherto known as Cow
453.06  Parlour off Cork street be henceforth designated Boulevard Bloom.</p>
453.07            <p><sc>councillor lorcan sherlock</sc></p>
453.08  <p>Carried unanimously.</p>
453.09            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
453.10  <p>(<i>Impassionedly.</i>) These flying Dutchmen or lying Dutchmen as they recline
453.11  in their upholstered poop, casting dice, what reck they? Machines is their cry,
453.12  their chimera, their panacea. Laboursaving apparatuses, supplanters, bugbears,
453.13  manufactured monsters for mutual murder, hideous hobgoblins produced by
453.14  a horde of capitalistic lusts upon our prostituted labour. The poor man starves
453.15  while they are grassing their royal mountain stags or shooting peasants and
453.16  phartridges in their purblind pomp of pelf and power. But their reign is rover
453.17  for rever and ever and ev ...</p>
453.18  <p>(<i>Prolonged applause. Venetian masts, maypoles and festal arches spring
453.19  up. A streamer bearing the legends</i> Cead Mile Failte <i>and</i> Mah Ttob
453.20  Melek Israel <i>spans the street. All the windows are thronged with
453.21  sightseers, chiefly ladies. Along the route the regiments of the royal
453.22  Dublin fusiliers, the King's own Scottish borderers, the Cameron
453.23  Highlanders and the Welsh Fusiliers, standing to attention keep back
453.24  the crowd. Boys from High school are perched on the lampposts, telegraph
453.25  poles, windowsills, cornices, gutters, chimneypots, railings, rainspouts,
453.26  whistling and cheering. The pillar of the cloud appears. A fife and
453.27  drum band is heard in the distance playing the Kol Nidre. The beaters

465.03  heaven, I am guiltless as the unsunned snow! It was my brother Henry. He
465.04  is my double. He lives in number 2 Dolphin's Barn. Slander, the viper, has
465.05  wrongfully accused me. Fellowcountrymen, <i>sgenl inn ban bata coisde gan capall.</i>
465.06  I call on my old friend, Dr Malachi Mulligan, sex specialist, to give medical
465.07  testimony on my behalf.</p>
465.08            <p><sc>dr mulligan</sc></p>
465.09  <p>(<i>In motor jerkin, green motorgoggles on his brow.</i>) Dr Bloom is bisexually
465.10  abnormal. He has recently escaped from Dr Eustace's private asylum for
465.11  demented gentlemen. Born out of bedlock hereditary epilepsy is present, the
465.12  consequence of unbridled lust. Traces of elephantiasis have been discovered
465.13  among his ascendants. There are marked symptoms of chronic exhibitionism.
465.14  Ambidexterity is also latent. He is prematurely bald from selfabuse, perversely
465.15  idealistic in consequence, a reformed rake, and has metal teeth. In consequence
465.16  of a family complex he has temporarily lost his memory and I believe him to
465.17  be more sinned against than sinning. I have made a pervaginal examination
465.18  and, after application of the acid test to 5427 anal, axillary, pectoral and
465.19  pubic hairs, I declare him to be <i>virgo intacta</i>.</p>
465.20  <p>(<i>Bloom holds his high grade hat over his genital organs.</i>)</p>
465.21            <p><sc>dr madden</sc></p>
465.22  <p>Hypsospadia is also marked. In the interest of coming generations I suggest
465.23  that the parts affected should be preserved in spirits of wine in the national
465.24  teratological museum.</p>
465.25            <p><sc>dr crotthers</sc></p>
465.26  <p>I have examined the patient's urine. It is albuminoid. Salivation is
465.27  insufficient, the patellar reflex intermittent.</p>
465.28            <p><sc>dr punch costello</sc></p>
465.29  <p>The <i>fetor judaicus</i> is most perceptible.</p>
465.30            <p><sc>dr dixon</sc></p>
465.31  <p>(<i>Reads a bill of health.</i>) Professor Bloom is a finished example of the new
465.32  womanly man. His moral nature is simple and lovable. Many have found
466.01  him a dear man, a dear person. He is a rather quaint fellow on the whole,
466.02  coy though not feebleminded in the medical sense. He has written a really
466.03  beautiful letter, a poem in itself, to the court missionary of the Reformed
466.04  Priests Protection Society which clears up everything. He is practically a total
466.05  abstainer and I can affirm that he sleeps on a straw litter and eats the most
466.06  Spartan food, cold dried grocer's peas. He wears a hairshirt winter and summer
466.07  and scourges himself every Saturday. He was, I understand, at one time a
466.08  firstclass misdemeanant in Glencree reformatory. Another report states that he
466.09  was a very posthumous child. I appeal for clemency in the name of the most
466.10  sacred word our vocal organs have ever been called upon to speak. He is about
466.11  to have a baby.</p>
466.12  <p>(<i>General commotion and compassion. Women faint. A wealthy American
466.13  makes a street collection for Bloom. Gold and silver coins, blank
466.14  cheques, banknotes, jewels, treasury bonds, maturing bills of exchange,
466.15  I.O.U's, wedding rings, watchchains, lockets, necklaces and bracelets
466.16  are rapidly collected.</i>)</p>

474.19            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
474.20  <p>As a matter of fact it is of no importance whether Benedetto Marcello
474.21  found it or made it. The rite is the poet's rest. It may be an old hymn to
474.22  Demeter or also illustrate <i>Cœla enarrant gloriam Domini</i>. It is susceptible of
474.23  nodes or modes as far apart as hyperphrygian and mixolydian and of texts so
474.24  divergent as priests haihooping round David's that is Circe's or what am I
474.25  saying Ceres' altar and David's tip from the stable to his chief bassoonist about
474.26  the alrightiness of his almightiness. <i>Mais, nom de nom,</i> that is another pair of
474.27  trousers. <i>Jetez la gourme. Faut que jeunesse se passe.</i> (<i>He stops, points at Lynch's cap,
474.28  smiles, laughs.</i>) Which side is your knowledge bump?</p>

496.01            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
496.02  <p>(<i>Cowed.</i>) Exuberant female. Enormously I desiderate your domination. I
496.03  am exhausted, abandoned, no more young. I stand, so to speak, with an
496.04  unposted letter bearing the extra regulation fee before the too late box of the
496.05  general postoffice of human life. The door and window open at a right angle
496.06  cause a draught of thirtytwo feet per second according to the law of falling
496.07  bodies. I have felt this instant a twinge of sciatica in my left glutear muscle. It
496.08  runs in our family. Poor dear papa, a widower, was a regular barometer from
496.09  it. He believed in animal heat. A skin of tabby lined his winter waistcoat.
496.10  Near the end, remembering king David and the Sunamite, he shared his bed

518.27  <p>Here. (<i>She hauls up a reef of her slip, revealing her bare thigh and unrolls the
518.28  potato from the top of her stocking.</i>) Those that hides knows where to find.</p>
519.01            <p><sc>bella</sc></p>
519.02  <p>(<i>Frowns.</i>) Here. This isn't a musical peepshow. And don't you smash that
519.03  piano. Who's paying here?</p>
519.04  <p>(<i>She goes to the pianola. Stephen fumbles in his pocket and, taking out a
519.05  banknote by its corner, hands it to her.</i>)</p>
519.06            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
519.07  <p>(<i>With exagerated politeness.</i>) This silken purse I made out of the sow's
519.08  ear of the public. Madam, excuse me. If you allow me. (<i>He indicates vaguely
519.09  Lynch and Bloom.</i>) We are all in the same sweepstake, Kinch and Lynch. <i>Dans
519.10  ce bordel où tenons nostre état.</i></p>
519.11            <p><sc>lynch</sc></p>
519.12  <p>(<i>Calls from the hearth.</i>) Dedalus! Give her your blessing for me.</p>
519.13            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
519.14  <p>(<i>Hands Bella a coin.</i>) Gold. She has it.</p>
519.15            <p><sc>bella</sc></p>
519.16  <p>(<i>Looks at the money, then at Zoe, Florrie and Kitty.</i>) Do you want three girls?
519.17  It's ten shillings here.</p>
519.18            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
519.19  <p>(<i>Delightedly.</i>) A hundred thousand apologies. (<i>He fumbles again and takes
519.20  out and hands her two crowns.</i>) Permit, <i>brevi manu</i>, my sight is somewhat
519.21  troubled.</p>
519.22  <p>(<i>Bella goes to the table to count the money while Stephen talks to himself
519.23  in monosyllabbes. Zoe bounds over to the table. Kitty leans over Zoe's
519.24  neck, Lynch gets up, rights his cap and clasping Kitty's waist, adds his
519.25  head to the group.</i>)</p>
519.26            <p><sc>florry</sc></p>
519.27  <p>(<i>Strives heavily to rise.</i>) Ow! My foot's asleep. (<i>She limps over to the table.
519.28  Bloom approaches.</i>)</p>
519.29            <p><sc>bella, zoe, kitty, lynch, bloom</sc></p>
519.30  <p>(<i>Chattering and squabbling.</i>) The gentleman ... ten shillings ... paying for the
519.31  three ... allow me a moment ... this gentleman pays separate ... who's touching
519.32  it? ... ow ... mind who you're pinching ... are you staying the night or a
520.01  short time? ... who did? ... you're a liar, excuse me ... the gentleman paid down
520.02  like a gentleman ... drink ... it's long after eleven.</p>
520.03            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
520.04  <p>(<i>At the pianola, making a gesture of abhorrence.</i>) No bottles! What,
520.05  eleven? A riddle.</p>
520.06            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
520.07  <p>(<i>Lifting up her pettigown and folding a half sovereign into the top of her
520.08  stocking.</i>) Hard earned on the flat of my back.</p>
520.09            <p><sc>lynch</sc></p>
520.10  <p>(<i>Lifting Kitty from the table.</i>) Come!</p>
520.11            <p><sc>kitty</sc></p>
520.12  <p>Wait. (<i>She clutches the two crowns.</i>)</p>
520.13            <p><sc>florry</sc></p>
520.14  <p>And me?</p>
520.15            <p><sc>lynch</sc></p>
520.16  <p>Hoopla!</p>
520.17  <p>(<i>He lifts her, carries her and bumps her down on the sofa.</i>)</p>
520.18            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
520.19  <p>The fox crew, the cocks flew,</p>
520.20  <p>The bells in heaven</p>
520.21  <p>Were striking eleven.</p>
520.22  <p>'Tis time for her poor soul</p>
520.23  <p>To get out of heaven.</p>
520.24            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
520.25  <p>(<i>Quietly lays a half sovereign on the table between Bella and Florry.</i>) So.
520.26  Allow me. (<i>He takes up the poundnote.</i>) Three times ten. We're square.</p>
520.27            <p><sc>bella</sc></p>
520.28  <p>(<i>Admiringly.</i>) You're such a slyboots, old cocky. I could kiss you.</p>
521.01            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
521.02  <p>(<i>Points.</i>) Hum? Deep as a drawwell. (<i>Lynch bends Kitty back over the sofa
521.03  and kisses her. Bloom goes with the poundnote to Stephen.</i>)</p>
521.04            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
521.05  <p>This is yours.</p>
521.06            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
521.07  <p>How is that? <i>Le distrait</i> or absentminded beggar. (<i>He fumbles again in his
521.08  pocket and draws out a handful of coins. An object falls.</i>) That fell.</p>
521.09            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
521.10  <p>(<i>Stooping, picks up and hands a box of matches.</i>) This.</p>
521.11            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
521.12  <p>Lucifer. Thanks.</p>
521.13            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
521.14  <p>(<i>Quietly.</i>) You had better hand over that cash to me to take care of. Why
521.15  pay more?</p>
521.16            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
521.17  <p>(<i>Hands him all his coins.</i>) Be just before you are generous.</p>
521.18            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
521.19  <p>I will but is it wise? (<i>He counts.</i>) One, seven, eleven, and five. Six.
521.20  Eleven. I don't answer for what you may have lost.</p>
521.21            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
521.22  <p>Why striking eleven? Proparoxyton. Moment before the next Lessing
521.23  says. Thirsty fox. (<i>He laughs loudly.</i>) Burying his grandmother. Probably he
521.24  killed her.</p>
521.25            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
521.26  <p>That is one pound six and eleven. One pound seven, say.</p>
521.27            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
521.28  <p>Doesn't matter a rambling damn.</p>
521.29            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
521.30  <p>No, but ...</p>
522.01            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
522.02  <p>(<i>Comes to the table.</i>) Cigarette, please. (<i>Lynch tosses a cigarette from the sofa
522.03  to the table.</i>) And so Georgina Johnson is dead and married. (<i>A cigarette appears
522.04  on the table Stephen looks at it.</i>) Wonder. Parlour magic. Married. Hm. (<i>He strikes
522.05  a match and proceeds to light the cigarette with enigmatic melancholy.</i>)</p>
522.06            <p><sc>lynch</sc></p>
522.07  <p>(<i>Watching him.</i>) You would have a better chance of lighting it if you held
522.08  the match nearer.</p>
522.09            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
522.10  <p>(<i>Brings the match nearer his eye.</i>) Lynx eye. Must get glasses. Broke them
522.11  yesterday. Sixteen years ago. Distance. The eye sees all flat. (<i>He draws the
522.12  match away. It goes out.</i>) Brain thinks. Near: far. Ineluctable modality of the
522.13  visible. (<i>He frowns mysteriously.</i>) Hm. Sphinx. The beast that has two backs at
522.14  midnight. Married.</p>
522.15            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
522.16  <p>It was a commercial traveller married her and took her away with him.</p>
522.17            <p><sc>florry</sc></p>
522.18  <p>(<i>Nods.</i>) Mr Lambe from London.</p>
522.19            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
522.20  <p>Lamb of London, who takest away the sins of our world.</p>
522.21            <p><sc>lynch</sc></p>
522.22  <p>(<i>Embracing Kitty on the sofa, chants deeply.</i>) <i>Dona nobis pacem.</i></p>
522.23  <p>(<i>The cigarette slips from Stephen's fingers. Bloom picks it up and throws
522.24  it into the gate.</i>)</p>
522.25            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
522.26  <p>Don't smoke. You ought to eat. Cursed dog I met. (<i>To Zoe.</i>) You have
522.27  nothing?</p>
522.28            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
522.29  <p>Is he hungry?</p>
523.01            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
523.02  <p>(<i>Extends his hand to her smiling and chants to the air of the bloodoath in the</i>
523.03  Dusk of the Gods.)</p>
523.04  <p>Hangende Hunger,</p>
523.05  <p>Fragende Frau,</p>
523.06  <p>Macht uns alle kaput.</p>
523.07            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
523.08  <p>(<i>Tragically.</i>) Hamlet, I am thy father's gimlet! (<i>She takes his hand.</i>) Blue
523.09  eyes beauty I'll read your hand. (<i>She points to his forehead.</i>) No wit, no wrinkles
523.10  (<i>She counts.</i>) Two, three, Mars, that's courage. (<i>Stephen shakes his head.</i>) No kid.</p>
523.11            <p><sc>lynch</sc></p>
523.12  <p>Sheet lightning courage. The youth who could not shiver and shake. (<i>To
523.13  Zoe.</i>) Who taught you palmistry?</p>
523.14            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
523.15  <p>(<i>Turns.</i>) Ask my ballocks that I haven't got. (<i>To Stephen.</i>) I see it in
523.16  your face. The eye, like that. (<i>She frowns with lowered head.</i>)</p>
523.17            <p><sc>lynch</sc></p>
523.18  <p>(<i>Laughing, slaps Kitty behind twice.</i>) Like that. Pandy bat.</p>
523.19  <p>(<i>Twice loudly a pandybat cracks, the coffin of the pianola flies open, the
523.20  bald tittle round jack-in-the-box head of Father Dolan springs up.</i>)</p>
523.21            <p><sc>father dolan</sc></p>
523.22  <p>Any boy want flogging? Broke his glasses? Lazy idle little schemer. See
523.23  it in your eye.</p>
523.24  <p>(<i>Mild, benign, rectorial, reproving, the head of Don John Connee rises
523.25  from the pianola coffin.</i>)</p>
523.26            <p><sc>don john connee</sc></p>
523.27  <p>Now, Father Dolan! Now. I'm sure that Stephen is a very good little
523.28  boy.</p>
523.29            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
523.30  <p>(<i>Examining Stephen's palm.</i>) Woman's hand.</p>
524.01            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
524.02  <p>(<i>Murmurs.</i>) Continue. Lie. Hold me. Caress. I never could read His
524.03  handwriting except His criminal thumbprint on the haddock.</p>
524.04            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
524.05  <p>What day were you born?</p>
524.06            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
524.07  <p>Thursday. Today.</p>
524.08            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
524.09  <p>Thursday's child has far to go. (<i>She traces lines on his hand.</i>) Line of fate.
524.10  Influential friends.</p>
524.11            <p><sc>florry</sc></p>
524.12  <p>(<i>Pointing.</i>) Imagination.</p>
524.13            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
524.14  <p>Mount of the moon. You'll meet with a ... (<i>She peers at his hands abruptly.</i>)
524.15  I won't tell you what's not good for you. Or do you want to know?</p>
524.16            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
524.17  <p>(<i>Detaches her fingers and offers his palm.</i>) More harm than good. Here. Read
524.18  mine.</p>
524.19            <p><sc>bella</sc></p>
524.20  <p>Show. (<i>She turns up Bloom's hand.</i>) I thought so. Knobby knuckles, for
524.21  the women.</p>
524.22            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
524.23  <p>(<i>Peering at Bloom's palm.</i>) Gridiron. Travels beyond the sea and marry
524.24  money.</p>
524.25            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
524.26  <p>Wrong.</p>
524.27            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
524.28  <p>(<i>Quickly.</i>) O, I see. Short little finger. Henpecked husband. That wrong?</p>
524.29  <p>(<i>Black Liz, a huge rooster hatching in a chalked circle, rises, stretches her
524.30  wings and clucks.</i>)</p>
525.01            <p><sc>black liz</sc></p>
525.02  <p>Gara. Klook. Klook. Klook.</p>
525.03  <p>(<i>She sidles from her newlaid egg and waddles off.</i>)</p>
525.04            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
525.05  <p>(<i>Points to his hand.</i>) That weal there is an accident. Fell and cut it twenty
525.06  two years age. I was sixteen.</p>
525.07            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
525.08  <p>I see, says the blind man. Tell us news.</p>
525.09            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
525.10  <p>See? Moves to one great goal. I am twentytwo too. Sixteen years ago I
525.11  twentytwo tumbled, twentytwo years ago he sixteen fell off his hobbyhorse
525.12  (<i>He winces.</i>) Hurt my hand somewhere. Must see a dentist. Money?</p>
525.13  <p>(<i>Zoe whispers to Florry. They giggle. Bloom releases his hand and writes
525.14  idly on the table in backhand, pencilling slow curves.</i>)</p>
525.15            <p><sc>florry</sc></p>
525.16  <p>What?</p>
525.17  <p>(<i>A hackneycar, number three hundred and twentyfour, with a gallant
525.18  buttocked mare, driven by James Barton, Harmony Avenue,
525.19  Donnybrook, trots past. Blazes Boylan and Lenehan sprawl swaying
525.20  on the sideseats. The Ormond boots crouches behind on the axle. Sadly
525.21  over the crossblind Lydia Douce and Mina Kennedy gaze.</i>)</p>
525.22            <p><sc>the boots</sc></p>
525.23  <p>(<i>Jogging, mocks them with thumb and wriggling wormfingers.</i>) Haw, haw,
525.24  have you the horn?</p>
525.25  <p>(<i>Bronze by gold they whisper.</i>).</p>
525.26            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
525.27  <p>(<i>To Florry.</i>) Whisper.</p>
525.28  <p>(<i>They whisper again.</i>)</p>
525.29  <p>(<i>Over the well of the car Blazes Boylan leans, his boater straw, set sideways,
525.30  a red flower in his mouth. Lenehan, in a yachtsman's cap and
526.01  white shoes, officiously detaches a long hair from Blazes Boylan's
526.02  shoulder.</i>)</p>
526.03            <p><sc>lenehan</sc></p>
526.04  <p>Ho! What do I here behold? Were you brushing the cobwebs off a few
526.05  quims?</p>
526.06            <p><sc>boylan</sc></p>
526.07  <p>(<i>Sated, smiles.</i>) Plucking a turkey.</p>
526.08            <p><sc>lenehan</sc></p>
526.09  <p>A good night's work.</p>
526.10            <p><sc>boylan</sc></p>
526.11  <p>(<i>Holding up four thick bluntungulated fingers, winks.</i>) Blazes Kate! Up to
526.12  sample or your money back. (<i>He holds out a forefinger.</i>) Smell that.</p>
526.13            <p><sc>lenehan</sc></p>
526.14  <p>(<i>Smells gleefully.</i>) Ah! Lobster and mayonnaise. Ah!</p>
526.15            <p><sc>zoe</sc> and <sc>florry</sc></p>
526.16  <p>(<i>Laugh together.</i>) Ha ha ha ha.</p>
526.17            <p><sc>boylan</sc></p>
526.18  <p>(<i>Jumps surely from the car and calls loudly for all to hear.</i>) Hello, Bloom!
526.19  Mrs Bloom up yet?</p>
526.20            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
526.21  <p>(<i>In a flunkey's plum plush coat and kneebreeches, buff stockings and powdered
526.22  wig.</i>) I'm afraid not, sir, the last articles .....</p>
526.23            <p><sc>boylan</sc></p>
526.24  <p>(<i>Tosses him sixpence.</i>) Here, to buy yourself a gin and splash. (<i>He hangs his
526.25  hat smartly on a peg of Bloom's autlered head.</i>) Show me in. I have a little private
526.26  business with your wife. You understand?</p>
526.27            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
526.28  <p>Thank you, sir. Yes, sir, Madam Tweedy is in her bath, sir.</p>
527.01            <p><sc>marion</sc></p>
527.02  <p>He ought to feel himself highly honoured. (<i>She plops splashing out of the
527.03  water.</i>) Raoul, darling, come and dry me. I'm in my pelt. Only my new hat
527.04  and a carriage sponge.</p>
527.05            <p><sc>boylan</sc></p>
527.06  <p>(<i>A merry twinkle in his eye.</i>) Topping!</p>
527.07            <p><sc>bella</sc></p>
527.08  <p>What? What is it?</p>
527.09  <p>(<i>Zoe whispers to her.</i>)</p>
527.10            <p><sc>marion</sc></p>
527.11  <p>Let him look, the pishogue! Pimp! And scourge himself! I'll write to
527.12  a powerful prostitute or Bartholomona, the bearded woman, to raise weals out
527.13  on him an inch thick and make him bring me back a signed and stamped receipt.</p>
527.14            <p><sc>bella</sc></p>
527.15  <p>(<i>Laughing.</i>) Ho ho ho ho.</p>
527.16            <p><sc>boylan</sc></p>
527.17  <p>(<i>To Bloom, over his shoulder.</i>) You can apply your eye to the keyhole and
527.18  play with yourself while I just go through her a few times.</p>
527.19            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
527.20  <p>Thank you, sir. I will, sir. May I bring two men chums to witness the deed
527.21  and take a snapshot? (<i>He holds an ointment jar.</i>) Vaseline, sir? Orangeflower? ...
527.22  Lukewarm water? ...</p>
527.23            <p><sc>kitty</sc></p>
527.24  <p>(<i>From the sofa.</i>) Tell us, Florry. Tell us. What ...</p>
527.25  <p>(<i>Florry whispers to her. Whispering lovewords murmur liplapping loudly,
527.26  poppysmic plopslop.</i>)</p>
527.27            <p><sc>mina kennedy</sc></p>
527.28  <p>(<i>Her eyes upturned.</i>) O, it must be like the scent of geraniums and lovely
527.29  peaches! O, he simply idolises every bit of her! Stuck together! Covered with
527.30  kisses!</p>
528.01            <p><sc>lydia douce</sc></p>
528.02  <p>(<i>Her mouth opening.</i>) Yumyum. O, he's carrying her round the room doing
528.03  it! Ride a cock horse. You could hear them in Paris and New York. Like
528.04  mouthfuls of strawberries and cream.</p>
528.05            <p><sc>kitty</sc></p>
528.06  <p>(<i>Laughing.</i>) Hee hee hee.</p>
528.07            <p><sc>boylan's voice</sc></p>
528.08  <p>(<i>Sweetly, hoarsely, in the pit of his stomach.</i>) Ah! Gooblazeqruk
528.09  brukarchkrasht!</p>
528.10            <p><sc>marion's voice</sc></p>
528.11  <p>(<i>Hoarsely, sweetly rising to her throat.</i>) O! Weeshwashtkissimapooisth-
528.12  napoohuck!</p>
528.13            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
528.14  <p>(<i>His eyes wildy dilated, clasps himself.</i>) Show! Hide! Show! Plough her!
528.15  More! Shoot!</p>
528.16            <p><sc>bella, zoe, florry, kitty</sc></p>
528.17  <p>Ho ho! Ha ha! Hee hee!</p>
528.18            <p><sc>lynch</sc></p>
528.19  <p>(<i>Points.</i>) The mirror up to nature. (<i>He laughs.</i>) Hu hu hu hu hu.</p>
528.20  <p>(<i>Stephen and Bloom gaze in the mirror. The face of William Shakespeare,
528.21  beardless, appears there, rigid in facial paralysis, crowned by the
528.22  reflection of the reindeer antlered hatrack in the hall.</i>)</p>
528.23            <p><sc>shakespeare</sc></p>
528.24  <p>(<i>In dignified ventriloquy.</i>) 'Tis the loud laugh bespeaks the vacant mind. (<i>To
528.25  Bloom.</i>) Thou thoughtest as how thou wastest invisible. Gaze. (<i>He crows with
528.26  a black capon's laugh.</i>) Iagogo! How my Oldfellow chokit his Thursdaymomun.
528.27  Iagogogo!</p>
528.28            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
528.29  <p>(<i>Smiles yellowly at the whores.</i>) When will I hear the joke?</p>
529.01            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
529.02  <p>Before you're twice married and once a widower.</p>
529.03            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
529.04  <p>Lapses are condoned. Even the great Napoleon, when measurements
529.05  were taken near the skin after his death ...</p>
529.06  <p>(<i>Mrs Dignam, widow woman, her snubnose and cheeks flushed with
529.07  deathtalk, fears and Tunny's tawny sherry, hurries by in her weeds,
529.08  her bonnet awry, rouging and powdering her cheeks, lips and nose a
529.09  pen chivvying her brood of cygnets. Beneath her skirt appear her late
529.10  husband's everyday trousers and turnedup boots, large eights. She
529.11  holds a Scottish widow's insurance policy and large marqueeumbrella
529.12  under which her brood runs with her, Patsy, hopping on one short foot,
529.13  his collar loose, a hank of porksteaks dangling, Freddy, whimpering,
529.14  Susy with a crying cods' mouth, Alice, struggling with the baby. She
529.15  cuffs them on, her streamers flaunting aloft.</i>)</p>
529.16            <p><sc>freddy</sc></p>
529.17  <p>Ah, ma, you're dragging me along!</p>
529.18            <p><sc>susy</sc></p>
529.19  <p>Mamma, the beeftea is fizzing over!</p>
529.20            <p><sc>shakespeare</sc></p>
529.21  <p>(<i>With paralytic rage.</i>) Weda seca whokilla farst.</p>
529.22  <p>(<i>The face of Martin Cunningham, bearded, refeatures Shakespeare's beardless
529.23  face. The marqueeumbrella sways drunkenly, the children run aside.
529.24  Under the umbrella appears Mrs Cunningham in Merry Widow hat
529.25  and kimono gown. She glides sidling and bowing, twisting japanesily.</i>)</p>
529.26            <p><sc>mrs cunningham</sc></p>
529.27  <p>(<i>Sings.</i>)</p>
529.28  <p>And they call me the jewel of Asia.</p>
529.29            <p><sc>martin cunningham</sc></p>
529.30  <p>(<i>Gazes on her impassive.</i>) Immense! Most bloody awful demirep!</p>
530.01            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
530.02  <p><i>Et exaltabuntur cornua iusti.</i> Queens lay with prize bulls. Remember
530.03  Pasiphae for whose lust my grandoldgrossfather made the first confessionbox.
530.04  Forget not Madam Grissel Steevens nor the suine scions of the house of
530.05  Lambert. And Noah was drunk with wine. And his ark was open.</p>
530.06            <p><sc>bella</sc></p>
530.07  <p>None of that here. Come to the wrong shop.</p>
530.08            <p><sc>lynch</sc></p>
530.09  <p>Let him alone. He's back from Paris.</p>
530.10            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>
530.11  <p>(<i>Runs to Stephen and links him.</i>) O go on! Give us some parleyvoo.</p>
530.12  <p>(<i>Stephen claps hat on head and leaps over to the fireplace, where he stands
530.13  with shrugged shoulders, finny hands outspread, a painted smile on
530.14  his face.</i>)</p>
530.15            <p><sc>lynch</sc></p>
530.16  <p>(<i>Pommelling on the sofa.</i>) Rmm Rmm Rmm Rrrrrrmmmmm.</p>
530.17            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
530.18  <p>(<i>Gabbles, with marionette jerks.</i>) Thousand places of entertainment to

542.01  sake! Inexpressible was my anguish when expiring with love, grief and agony

544.07            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>

544.11            <p><sc>zoe</sc></p>

544.13            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>

544.16  <p>(<i>He hurries out through the hall. The whores point. Florry follows, spilling
544.17  water from her tilted tumbler. On the doorstep all the whores clustered
544.18  talk volubly, pointing to the right where the fog has cleared off. From the
544.19  left arrives a jingling hackney car. It slows to in front of the house. Bloom
544.20  at the halldoor perceives Corny Kelleher who is about to dismount from
544.21  the car with two silent lechers. He averts his face. Bella from within
544.22  the hall urges on her whores. They blow ickylickysticky yumyum
544.23  kisses. Corny Kelleher replies with a ghostly lewd smile. The silent
544.24  lechers turn to pay the jarvey. Zoe and Kitty still point right. Bloom,
544.25  parting them swiftly, draws his caliph's hood and poncho and hurries
544.26  down the steps with sideways face. Incog Haroun al Raschid, he flits
544.27  behind the silent lechers and hastens on by the railings with fleet step
544.28  of a pard strewing the drag behind him, torn envelopes drenched in
544.29  aniseed. The ashplant marks his stride. A pack of bloodhounds led by
544.30  Hornblower of Trinity brandishing a dogwhip in tallyho cap, and
544.31  an old pair of grey trousers, follows from far, picking up the scent,
544.32  nearer, baying, panting, at fault, breaking away, throwing their
544.33  tongues, biting his heels, leaping at his tail. He walks, runs, zigzags,
545.01  gallops, lugs laid back. He is pelted with gravel, cabbagestumps,

548.20  <p>(<i>Edward the Seventh appears in an archway. He wears a white jersey on
548.21  which an image of the Sacred Heart is stitched, with the insignia of
548.22  Garter and Thistle, Golden Fleece, Elephant of Denmark, Skinner's
548.23  and Probyn's horse, Lincoln's Inns' bencher and ancient and
548.24  honourable artillery company of Massachussets. He sucks a red jujube.

548.27  plasterer's bucket on which is printed:</i> Défense d'uriner. <i>A roar of

548.29            <p><sc>edward the seventh</sc></p>
548.30  <p>(<i>Slowly, solemnly but indistinctly.</i>) Peace, perfect peace. For identification
548.31  bucket in my hand. Cheerio, boys. (<i>He turns to his subjects.</i>) We have come
549.01  here to witness a clean straight fight and we heartily wish both men the best
549.02  of good luck. Mahak makar a back.</p>
549.03  <p>(<i>He shakes hands with Private Carr, Private Compton, Stephen, Bloom

549.05  graciously in acknowledgement.</i>)</p>
549.06            <p><sc>private carr</sc></p>
549.07  <p>(<i>To Stephen.</i>) Say it again.</p>
549.08            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
549.09  <p>(<i>Nervous, friendly, pulls himself up.</i>) I understand your point of view though
549.10  I have no king myself for the moment. This is the age of patent medicine.
549.11  A discussion is difficult down here. But this is the point. You die for your
549.12  country, suppose. (<i>He places his arm on Private Carr's sleeve.</i>) Not that I wish
549.13  it for you. But I say: Let my country die for me. Up to the present it has done
549.14  so. I don't want it to die. Damn death. Long live life!</p>
549.15            <p><sc>edward the seventh</sc></p>
549.16  <p>(<i>Levitates over heaps of slain in the garb and with the halo of Joking Jesus, a

552.21  <p>(<i>The women's heads coalesce. Old Gummy Granny in sugarloaf hat

552.24            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>

552.27            <p><sc>old gummy granny</sc></p>
552.28  <p>(<i>Rocking to and fro.</i>) Ireland's sweetheart, the king of Spain's daughter,
552.29  alanna. Strangers im my house, bad manners to them! (<i>She keens with banshee
553.01  woe.</i>) Ochone! Ochone! Silk of the kine! (<i>She wails.</i>) You met with poor
553.02  old Ireland and how does she stand?</p>
553.03            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
553.04  <p>How do I stand you? The hat trick! Where's the third person of the
553.05  Blessed Trinity? Soggarth Aroon? The reverend Carrion Crow.</p>
553.06            <p><sc>cissy caffrey</sc></p>
553.07  <p>(<i>Shrill.</i>) Stop them from fighting!</p>
553.08            <p><sc>a rough</sc></p>
553.09  <p>Our men retreated.</p>
553.10            <p><sc>private carr</sc></p>
553.11  <p>(<i>Tugging at his belt.</i>) I'll wring the neck of any bugger says a word against
553.12  my fucking king.</p>
553.13            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
553.14  <p>(<i>Terrified.</i>) He said nothing. Not a word. A pure misunderstanding.</p>
553.15            <p><sc>the citizen</sc></p>
553.16  <p><i>Erin go hragh!</i></p>
553.17  <p>(<i>Major Tweedy and the Citizen exhibit to each other medals, decorations,
553.18  trophies of war, wounds. Both salute with fierce hostility.</i>)</p>
553.19            <p><sc>private compton</sc></p>
553.20  <p>Go it, Harry. Do him one in the eye. He's a proboer.</p>
553.21            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
553.22  <p>Did I? When?</p>
553.23            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
553.24  <p>(<i>To the redcoats.</i>) We fought for you in South Africa, Irish missile troops.
553.25  Isn't that history? Royal Dublin Fusiliers. Honoured by our monarch.</p>
553.26            <p><sc>the navvy</sc></p>
553.27  <p>(<i>Staggering past.</i>) O, yes. O, God, yes! O, make the kwawr a krowawr!
553.28  O! Bo!</p>
553.29  <p>(<i>Casqued halberdiers in armour thrust forward a pentice of gutted spear
553.30  points. Major Tweedy, moustached like Turko the terrible, in bearskin
554.01  cap with hackle plume and accoutrements, with epaulette, gilt chevrons
554.02  and sabretache, his breast bright with medals, toes the line. He gives
554.03  the pilgrim warrior's sign of the knights templars.</i>)</p>
554.04            <p><sc>major tweedy</sc></p>
554.05  <p>(<i>Growls gruffly.</i>) Rorke's Drift! Up, guards, and at them! Mahal shalal
554.06  hashbaz.</p>
554.07            <p><sc>private carr</sc></p>
554.08  <p>I'll do him in.</p>
554.09            <p><sc>private compton</sc></p>
554.10  <p>(<i>Waves the crowd back.</i>) Fair play, here. Make a bleeding butcher's shop of
554.11  the bugger.</p>
554.12  <p>(<i>Massed bands blare</i> Garryowen <i>and</i> God save the king.)</p>
554.13            <p><sc>cissy caffrey</sc></p>
554.14  <p>They're going to fight. For me!</p>
554.15            <p><sc>cunty kate</sc></p>
554.16  <p>The brave and the fair.</p>
554.17            <p><sc>biddy the clap</sc></p>
