554.19            <p><sc>cunty kate</sc></p>
554.20  <p>(<i>Blushing deeply.</i>) Nay, Madam. The gules doublet and merry Saint
554.21  George for me!</p>
554.22            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
554.23  <p>The harlot's cry from street to street</p>
554.24  <p>Shall weave old Ireland's windingsheet.</p>
554.25            <p><sc>private carr</sc></p>
554.26  <p>(<i>Loosening his belt, shouts.</i>) I'll wring the neck of any fucking bastard says
554.27  a word against my bleeding fucking king.</p>
554.28            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
554.29  <p>(<i>Shakes Cissy Caffrey's shoulders.</i>) Speak, you! Are you struck dumb? You
555.01  are the link between nations and generations. Speak, woman, sacred life
555.02  giver!</p>
555.03            <p><sc>cissy caffrey</sc></p>
555.04  <p>(<i>Alarmed, seizes Private Carr's sleeve.</i>) Amn't I with you? Amn't I your
555.05  girl? Cissy's your girl. (<i>She cries.</i>) Police!</p>
555.06            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
555.07  <p>(<i>Ecstatically, to Cissy Caffrey.</i>)</p>
555.08  <p>White thy fambles, red thy gan</p>
555.09  <p>And thy quarrons dainty is.</p>
555.10            <p><sc>voices</sc></p>
555.11  <p>Police!</p>
555.12            <p><sc>distant voices</sc></p>
555.13  <p>Dublin's burning! Dublin's burning! On fire, on fire!</p>
555.14  <p>(<i>Brimstone fires spring up. Dense clouds roll past. Heavy Gatling guns
555.15  boom. Pandemonium. Troops deploy. Gallop of hoofs. Artillery.
555.16  Hoarse commands. Bells clang. Backers shout. Drunkards bawl
555.17  Whores screech. Foghorns hoot. Cries of valour. Shrieks of dying.
555.18  Pikes clash on cuirasses. Thieves rob the slain. Birds of prey, winging
555.19  from tbe sea, rising from marshlands, swooping from eyries, hover
555.20  screaming, gannets, cormorants, vultures, goshawks, climbing
555.21  woodcocks, peregrines, merlins, blackgrouse, sea eagles, gulls, albatrosses,
555.22  barnacle geese. The midnight sun is darkened. The earth trembles.
555.23  The dead of Dublin from Prospect and Mount Jerome in white
555.24  sheepskin overcoats and black goatfell cloaks arise and appear to many.
555.25  A chasm opens with a noisless yawn. Tom Rochford, winner in
555.26  athlete's singlet and breeches, arrives at the head of the national hurdle
555.27  handicap and leaps into the void. He is followed by a race of runners
555.28  and leapers. In wild attitudes they spring from the brink. Their bodies
555.29  plunge. Factory lasses with fancy clothes toss redhot Yorkshire
555.30  baraabombs. Society ladies lift their skirts above their heads to protect
555.31  themselves. Laughing witches in red cutty sarks ride through the air
555.32  on broomsticks. Quakerlyster plasters blisters. It rains dragon's teeth.
555.33  Armed heroes spring up from furrows. They exchange in amity
556.01  the pass of knights of the red cross and fight duels with cavalry sabres:
556.02  Wolfe Tome against Henry Grattan, Smith O'Brien against Daniel
556.03  O'Connell, Michael Davitt against Isaac Butt, Justin M'Carthy
556.04  against Parnell, Arthur Griffith against John Redmond, John O'Leary
556.05  against Lear O'Johnny, Lord Edward Fitzgerald against Lord
556.06  Gerald Fitzedward, The O'Donoghue of the Glens against The Glens
556.07  of The Donoghue. On an eminence, the centre of the earth, rises the field
556.08  altar of Saint Barbara. Black candles rise from its gospel and epistle
556.09  horns. From the high barbacans of the tower two shafts of light fall
556.10  on the smokepalled altarstone. On the altarstone Mrs Mina Purefoy,
556.11  goddess of unreason, lies, naked, fettered, a chalice resting on her
556.12  swollen belly. Father Malachi O'Flynn in a long petticoat and reversed
556.13  chasuble, his two left feet back to the front, celebrates camp mass. The
556.14  Reverend Mr Hugh C Haines Love M.A. in a plain cassock and
556.15  mortar board, his head and collar back to the front, holds over the
556.16  celebrant's head an open umbrella.</i>)</p>
556.17            <p><sc>father malachi o'flynn</sc></p>
556.18  <p><i>Introibo ad altare diaboli.</i></p>
556.19            <p><sc>the reverend mr haines love</sc></p>
556.20  <p>To the devil which hath made glad my young days.</p>
556.21            <p><sc>father malachi o'flynn</sc></p>
556.22  <p>(<i>Takes from the chalice and elevates a blooddripping host.</i>) <i>Corpus Meum.</i></p>
556.23            <p><sc>the reverend mr haines love</sc></p>
556.24  <p>(<i>Raises high behind the celebrant's petticoats, revealing his grey bare hairy
556.25  buttocks between which a carrot is stuck.</i>) My body.</p>
556.26            <p><sc>the voice of all the damned</sc></p>
556.27  <p>Htengier Lnetopinmo Dog Drol eht rof, Aiulella!</p>
556.28  <p>(<i>From on high the voice of Adonai calls.</i>)</p>

557.01            <p><sc>the voice of all the blessed</sc></p>

557.03  <p>(<i>From on high the voice of Adonai calls.</i>)</p>

557.06  <p>(<i>In strident discord peasants and townsmen of Orange and Green factions

557.08            <p><sc>private carr</sc></p>
557.09  <p>(<i>With ferocious articulation.</i>) I'll do him in, so help me fucking Christ!
557.10  I'll wring the bastard fucker's bleeding blasted fucking windpipe!</p>
557.11            <p><sc>old gummy granny</sc></p>
557.12  <p>(<i>Thrusts a dagger towards Stephen's hand.</i>) Remove him, acushla. At 8.35

557.14  take him!</p>
557.15            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>

557.23            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>

557.25  your stick.</p>
557.26            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
557.27  <p>Stick, no. Reason. This feast of pure reason.</p>
557.28            <p><sc>cissy caffrey</sc></p>
557.29  <p>(<i>Pulling Private Carr.</i>) Come on, you're boosed. He insulted me but
557.30  I forgive him. (<i>Shouting in his ear.</i>) I forgive him for insulting me.</p>
557.31            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
558.01  <p>(<i>Over Stephen's shoulder.</i>) Yes, go. You see he's incapable.</p>
558.02            <p><sc>private carr</sc></p>
558.03  <p>(<i>Breaks loose.</i>) I'll insult him.</p>
558.04  <p>(<i>He rushes towards Stephen, fists outstretched, and strikes him in the face.
558.05  Stephen totters, collapses, falls stunned. He lies prone, his face to the
558.06  sky, his hat rolling to the wall. Bloom follows and picks it up.</i>)</p>
558.07            <p><sc>major tweedy</sc></p>
558.08  <p>(<i>Loudly.</i>) Carbine in bucket! Cease fire! Salute!</p>

558.11            <p><sc>the crowd</sc></p>
558.12  <p>Let him up! Don't strike him when he's down! Air! Who? The soldier
558.13  hit him. He's a professor. Is he hurted? Don't manhandle him! he's fainted!</p>
558.14  <p>(<i>The retriever, nosing on the fringe of the crowd, barks noisily.</i>)</p>
558.15            <p><sc>a hag</sc></p>
558.16  <p>What call had the redcoat to strike the gentleman and he under the
558.17  influence. Let them go and fight the Boers!</p>
558.18            <p><sc>the bawd</sc></p>

558.20  gave him the coward's blow.</p>

558.24            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>

559.01            <p><sc>private compton</sc></p>
559.02  <p>(<i>Tugging his comrade.</i>) Here bugger off, Harry. There's the cops! (<i>Two
559.03  raincaped watch, tall, stand in the group.</i>)</p>
559.04            <p><sc>first watch</sc></p>
559.05  <p>What's wrong here?</p>
559.06            <p><sc>private compton</sc></p>

559.08  retriever barks.</i>) Who owns the bleeding tyke?</p>
559.09            <p><sc>cissy caffrey</sc></p>
559.10  <p>(<i>With expectation.</i>) Is he bleeding?</p>
559.11            <p><sc>a man</sc></p>

559.13            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
559.14  <p>(<i>Glances sharply at the man.</i>) Leave him to me. I can easily ...</p>
559.15            <p><sc>second watch</sc></p>
559.16  <p>Who are you? Do you know him?</p>
559.17            <p><sc>private carr</sc></p>

559.26  the lockup.</p>
560.01            <p><sc>private carr</sc></p>
560.02  <p>(<i>Staggering as he is pulled away.</i>) God fuck old Bennett! He's a whitearsed
560.03  bugger. I don't give a shit for him.</p>
560.04            <p><sc>first watch</sc></p>
560.05  <p>(<i>Taking out his notebook.</i>) What's his name?</p>
560.06            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
560.07  <p>(<i>Peering over the crowd.</i>) I just see a car there. If you give me a hand a
560.08  second, sergeant ...</p>
560.09            <p><sc>first watch</sc></p>
560.10  <p>Name and address.</p>
560.11  <p>(<i>Corny Kelleher, weepers round his hat, a death wreath in his hand, appears
560.12  among the bystanders.</i>)</p>
560.13            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
560.14  <p>(<i>Quickly.</i>) O, the very man! (<i>He whispers.</i>) Simon Dedalus' son. A bit
560.15  sprung. Get those policemen to move those loafers back.</p>
560.16            <p><sc>second watch</sc></p>
560.17  <p>Night, Mr Kelleher.</p>
560.18            <p><sc>corny kelleher</sc></p>
560.19  <p>(<i>To the watch, with drawling eye.</i>) That's all right. I know him. Won a
560.20  bit on the races. Gold cup. Throwaway. (<i>He laughs.</i>) Twenty to one. Do you
560.21  follow me?</p>
560.22            <p><sc>first watch</sc></p>
560.23  <p>(<i>Turns to the crowd.</i>) Here, what are you all gaping at? Move on out of
560.24  that.</p>
560.25  <p>(<i>The crowd disperses slowly, muttering, down the lane.</i>)</p>
560.26            <p><sc>corny kelleher</sc></p>
560.27  <p>Leave it to me, sergeant. That'll be all right. (<i>He laughs, shaking his head.</i>)
560.28  We were often as bad ourselves, ay or worse. What? Eh, what?</p>
560.29            <p><sc>first watch</sc></p>
560.30  <p>(<i>Laughs.</i>) I suppose so.</p>
561.01            <p><sc>corny kelleher</sc></p>
561.02  <p>(<i>Nudges the second watch.</i>) Come and wipe your name off the slate. (<i>He
561.03  lilts, wagging his head.</i>) With my tooraloom tooraloom tooraloom tooraloom.
561.04  What, eh, do you follow me?</p>
561.05            <p><sc>second watch</sc></p>
561.06  <p>(<i>Genially.</i>) Ah, sure we were too.</p>
561.07            <p><sc>corny kelleher</sc></p>
561.08  <p>(<i>Winking.</i>) Boys will be boys. I've a car round there.</p>
561.09            <p><sc>second watch</sc></p>
561.10  <p>All right, Mr Kelleher. Good night.</p>
561.11            <p><sc>corny kelleher</sc></p>
561.12  <p>I'll see to that.</p>
561.13            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
561.14  <p>(<i>Shakes hands with both of the watch in turn.</i>) Thank you very much,
561.15  gentlemen, thank you. (<i>He mumbles confidentially.</i>) We don't want any scandal,
561.16  you understand. Father is a well known, highly respected citizen. Just a little
561.17  wild oats, you understand.</p>
561.18            <p><sc>first watch</sc></p>
561.19  <p>O, I understand, sir.</p>
561.20            <p><sc>second watch</sc></p>
561.21  <p>That's all right, sir.</p>
561.22            <p><sc>first watch</sc></p>
561.23  <p>It was only in case of corporal injuries I'd have to report it at the station.</p>
561.24            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
561.25  <p>(<i>Nods rapidly.</i>) Naturally. Quite right. Only your bounden duty.</p>
561.26            <p><sc>second watch</sc></p>
561.27  <p>It's our duty.</p>
561.28            <p><sc>corny kelleher</sc></p>
561.29  <p>Good night, men.</p>
562.01            <p><sc>the watch</sc></p>
562.02  <p>(<i>Saluting together.</i>) Night, gentlemen. (<i>They move off with slow heavy tread.</i>)</p>
562.03            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
562.04  <p>(<i>Blows.</i>) Providential you came on the scene. You have a car? ...</p>
562.05            <p><sc>corny kelleher</sc></p>
562.06  <p>(<i>Laughs, pointing his thumb over his right shoulder to the car brought up
562.07  against the scaffolding.</i>) Two commercials that were standing fizz in Jammet's.
562.08  Like princes, faith. One of them lost two quid on the race. Drowning his grief
562.09  and were on for a go with the jolly girls. So I landed them up on Behan's car
562.10  and down to nighttown.</p>
562.11            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
562.12  <p>I was just going home by Gardiner street when I happened to ...</p>
562.13            <p><sc>corny kelleher</sc></p>
562.14  <p>(<i>Laughs.</i>) Sure they wanted me to join in with the mots. No, by God,
562.15  says I. Not for old stagers like myself and yourself. (<i>He laughs again and leers
562.16  with lacklustre eye.</i>) Thanks be to God we have it in the house what, eh, do
562.17  you follow me? Hah! hah! hah!</p>
562.18            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
562.19  <p>(<i>Tries to laugh.</i>) He, he, he! Yes. Matter of fact I was just visiting an old
562.20  friend of mine there, Virag, you don't know him (poor fellow he's laid up
562.21  for the past week) and we had a liquor together and I was just making my
562.22  way home ...</p>
562.23  <p>(<i>The horse neighs.</i>)</p>
562.24            <p><sc>the horse</sc></p>
562.25  <p>Hohohohohohoh! Hohohohome!</p>
562.26            <p><sc>corny kelleher</sc></p>
562.27  <p>Sure it was Behan, our jarvey there, that told me after we left the two
562.28  commercials in Mrs Cohen's and I told him to pull up and got off to see. (<i>He
562.29  laughs.</i>) Sober hearsedrivers a specialty. Will I give him a lift home? Where
562.30  does he hang out? Somewhere in Cabra, what?</p>
563.01            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
563.02  <p>No, in Sandycove, I believe, from what he let drop.</p>
563.03  <p>(<i>Stephen, prone, breathes to the stars. Corny Kelleher, asquint, drawls at the
563.04  horse. Bloom in gloom, looms down.</i>)</p>
563.05            <p><sc>corny kelleher</sc></p>
563.06  <p>(<i>Scratches his nape.</i>) Sandycove! (<i>He bends down and calls to Stephen.</i>) Eh!
563.07  (<i>He calls again.</i>) Eh! He's covered with shavings anyhow. Take care they
563.08  didn't lift anything off him.</p>
563.09            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
563.10  <p>No, no, no. I have his money and his hat here and stick.</p>
563.11            <p><sc>corny kelleher</sc></p>
563.12  <p>Ah, well he'll get over it. No bones broken. Well, I'll shove along. (<i>He
563.13  laughs.</i>) I've a rendezvous in the morning. Burying the dead. Safe home!</p>
563.14            <p><sc>the horse</sc></p>
563.15  <p>(<i>Neighs.</i>) Hohohohohome.</p>
563.16            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
563.17  <p>Good night. I'll just wait and take him along in a few ...</p>
563.18  <p>(<i>Corny Kelleher returns to the outside car and mounts it. The horse
563.19  harness jingles.</i>)</p>
563.20            <p><sc>corny kelleher</sc></p>
563.21  <p>(<i>From the car, standing.</i>) Night.</p>
563.22            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
563.23  <p>Night.</p>
563.24  <p>(<i>The jarvey chucks the reins and raises his whip encouragingly. The
563.25  car and horse back slowly, awkwardly and turn. Corny Kelleher on
563.26  the sideseat sways his head to and fro in sign of mirth at Bloom's plight.
563.27  The jarvey joins in the mute pantomimic merriment nodding from
563.28  the farther seat. Bloom shakes his head in mute mirthful reply. With
563.29  thumb and palm Corny Kelleher reassures that the two bobbies will
563.30  allow the sleep to continue for what else is to be done. With a slow
564.01  nod Bloom conveys his gratitude as that is exactly what Stephen
564.02  needs. The car jingles tooraloom round the corner of the tooraloom
564.03  lane. Corny Kelleher again reassuralooms with his hand. Bloom with
564.04  his hand assuralooms Corny Kelleher that he is reassuraloomtay. The
564.05  tinkling hoofs and jingling harness grow fainter with their tooralooloo
564.06  looloo lay. Bloom, holding in his hand Stephen's hat festooned with
564.07  shavings and ashplant, stands irresolute. Then he bends to him and
564.08  shakes him by the shoulder.</i>)</p>
564.09            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
564.10  <p>Eh! Ho! (<i>There is no answer; he bends again.</i>) Mr Dedalus! (<i>There is no
564.11  answer.</i>) The name if you call. Somnambulist. (<i>He bends again and, hesitating,
564.12  brings his mouth near the face of the prostrate form.</i>) Stephen! (<i>There is no
564.13  answer. He calls again.</i>) Stephen!</p>
564.14            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
564.15  <p>(<i>Groans.</i>) Who? Black panther vampire. (<i>He sighs and stretches himself,
564.16  then murmurs thickly with prolonged vowels.</i>)</p>
564.17  <p>Who ... drive ... Fergus now.</p>
564.18  <p>And pierce ... wood's woven shade? ...</p>
564.19  <p>(<i>He turns on his left side, sighing, doubling himself together.</i>)</p>
564.20            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
564.21  <p>Poetry. Well educated. Pity. (<i>He bends again and undoes the buttons of
564.22  Stephen's waistcoat.</i>) To breathe. (<i>He brushes the woodshavings from Stephen's clothes
564.23  with light hands and fingers.</i>) One pound seven. Not hurt anyhow. (<i>He listens.</i>)
564.24  What!</p>
564.25            <p><sc>stephen</sc></p>
564.26  <p>(<i>Murmurs.</i>)</p>
564.27  <p>... shadows ... the woods.</p>
564.28  <p>... white breast ... dim ...</p>
564.29  <p>(<i>He stretches out his arms, sighs again and curls his body. Bloom holding
564.30  his hat and ashplant stands erect. A dog barks in the distance. Bloom
564.31  tightens and loosens his grip on the ashplant. He looks down on
564.32  Stephen's face and form.</i>)</p>
565.01            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
565.02  <p>(<i>Communes with the night.</i>) Face reminds me of his poor mother. In the
565.03  shady wood. The deep white breast. Ferguson, I think I caught. A girl. Some
565.04  girl. Best thing could happen him ... (<i>He murmurs.</i>) ... swear that I will always
565.05  hail, ever conceal, never reveal, any part or parts, art or arts ... (<i>He murmurs.</i>) ...
565.06  in the rough sands of the sea ... a cabletow's length from the shore ... where
565.07  the tide ebbs ... and flows ...</p>
565.08  <p>(<i>Silent, thoughtful, alert, he stands on guard, his fingers at his lips in
565.09  the attitude of secret master. Against the dark wall a figure appears
565.10  slowly, a fairy boy of eleven, a changeling, kidnapped, dressed in an
565.11  Eton suit with glass shoes and a little bronze helmet, holding a book
565.12  in his hand. He reads from right to left inaudibly, smiling, kissing the
565.13  page.</i>)</p>
565.14            <p><sc>bloom</sc></p>
565.15  <p>(<i>Wonderstruck, calls inaudibly.</i>) Rudy!</p>
565.16            <p><sc>rudy</sc></p>
565.17  <p>(<i>Gazes unseeing into Bloom's eyes and goes on reading, kissing, smiling.
565.18  He has a delicate mauve face. On his suit he has diamond and ruby
565.19  buttons. In his free left hand he holds a slim ivory cane with a violet
565.20  bowknot. A white lambskin peeps out of his waistcoat pocket.</i>)</p>
